# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api`, `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd`

# Kubernetes Admission Webhook Processing Chain

## Your Task

Trace the admission webhook processing chain in Kubernetes. Find Go source files across kubernetes/kubernetes and kubernetes/api that implement: the generic Webhook dispatcher (in pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/), the mutating webhook dispatcher with reinvocation logic, the validating webhook dispatcher with parallel dispatch, the WebhookAccessor abstraction layer, and the MutatingWebhookConfiguration/ValidatingWebhookConfiguration API type definitions.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

43-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced the Kubernetes admission webhook processing chain and created a comprehensive analysis document. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Components Identified:

### **Generic Webhook Framework** (`generic/`)
- `webhook.go`: Core `Webhook` struct with dispatch logic and hook matching
- `interfaces.go`: Defines `Dispatcher`, `Source`, `WebhookInvocation`, and `VersionedAttributeAccessor` interfaces

### **WebhookAccessor Abstraction** (`accessors.go`)
- Unified interface for both mutating and validating webhooks
- Implementations: `mutatingWebhookAccessor` and `validatingWebhookAccessor`

### **Mutating Webhook Pipeline** (`mutating/`)
- **Serial processing** with reinvocation support
- Tracks state using `webhookReinvokeContext` 
- Applies JSON patches to objects
- Located in: `plugin.go` and `dispatcher.go`

### **Validating Webhook Pipeline** (`validating/`)
- **Parallel dispatch** using `sync.WaitGroup` and goroutines
- Pre-caches versioned attributes
- Includes panic recovery per goroutine
- Located in: `plugin.go` and `dispatcher.go`

### **Configuration Management** (`configuration/`)
- `mutatingWebhookConfigurationManager`: Manages `MutatingWebhookConfiguration` resources
- `validatingWebhookConfigurationManager`: Manages `ValidatingWebhookConfiguration` resources
- Implements lazy evaluation with CEL expression caching

### **API Definitions** (`kubernetes-api/admissionregistration/v1/` and `v1beta1/`)
- `MutatingWebhookConfiguration` and `ValidatingWebhookConfiguration` types
- `MutatingWebhook` and `ValidatingWebhook` individual webhook specifications

The analysis document has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file listings, symbol definitions, execution chain, and detailed narrative explaining the archite

If the object is another cluster scoped resource,\n831: \t// it never skips the webhook.\n832: \t//\n833: \t// For example, to run the webhook on any objects whose namespace is not\n834: \t// associated with \"runlevel\" of \"0\" or \"1\";  you will set the selector as\n835: \t// follows:\n836: \t// \"namespaceSelector\": {\n837: \t//   \"matchExpressions\": [\n838: \t//     {\n839: \t//       \"key\": \"runlevel\",\n840: \t//       \"operator\": \"NotIn\",\n841: \t//       \"values\": [\n842: \t//         \"0\",\n843: \t//         \"1\"\n844: \t//       ]\n845: \t//     }\n846: \t//   ]\n847: \t// }\n848: \t//\n849: \t// If instead you want to only run the webhook on any objects whose\n850: \t// namespace is associated with the \"environment\" of \"prod\" or \"staging\";\n851: ",

This is an abstract admission plugin that provides common infrastructure for both mutating and validating webhooks. The key methods are:\\n\\n- `Dispatch()`: Routes webhook calls to the appropriate dispatcher based on admission attributes\\n- `ShouldCallHook()`: Determines whether a specific webhook should be invoked by checking namespace selectors, object selectors, rules, and match conditions\\n\\nThe `generic/interfaces.go` file defines critical abstractions:\\n- `Dispatcher`: An interface for dispatching webhook calls to a list of webhooks\\n- `Source`: Provides dynamic list of webhooks from configurations\\n- `WebhookInvocation`: Describes how to call a webhook, including resource and subresource information\\n- `VersionedAttributeAccessor`: Manages versioned attributes for different webhook kinds\\n\\n## WebhookAccessor Abstraction Layer\\n\\nIn `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/accessors.go`, the `WebhookAccessor` interface provides a unified abstraction for both mutating and validating webhooks. This abstraction allows code to work with either type without type-specific logic. Key implementations include:\\n\\n- `mutatingWebhookAccessor`: Wraps `v1.MutatingWebhook` objects\\n- `validatingWebhookAccessor`: Wraps `v1.ValidatingWebhook` objects\\n\\nFactory functions `NewMutatingWebhookAccessor` and `NewValidatingWebhookAccessor` create appropriately typed accessors with cached label selectors and compiled match conditions.\\n\\n## Mutating Webhook Pipeline\\n\\nThe mutating webhook pipeline starts in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/plugin.go`, where the `Plugin` struct embeds the generic `Webhook`. The `Admit()` method calls the generic `Dispatch()`, which delegates to `mutatingDispatcher`.\\n\\nThe `mutatingDispatcher` in `dispatcher.go` implements reinvocation logic for mutating webhooks:\\n- Uses `webhookReinvokeContext` to track which webhooks have been invoked\\n- Implements the `ReinvocationPolicy` mechanism to support re-invocation when mutations occur\\n- Processes webhooks serially (one after another) to ensure predictable mutation ordering\\n- Applies JSON patches from webhook responses to the object\\n- Tracks patch audit annotations for each webhook invocation\\n- Supports failure policy (Ignore or Fail)\\n\\nKey algorithm: The dispatcher iterates through hooks, calls `ShouldCallHook()` for each, and if eligible, calls `callAttrMutatingHook()` which constructs the AdmissionReview, sends it to the webhook endpoint, verifies the response, and applies any patches to the request object.\\n\\n## Validating Webhook Pipeline\\n\\nThe validating webhook pipeline starts in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/plugin.go`, similar to mutating. However, the `validatingDispatcher` in `dispatcher.go` uses **parallel dispatch** via goroutines:\\n\\n- Creates a list of relevant hooks by pre-filtering with `ShouldCallHook()`\\n- Pre-caches all versioned attributes to avoid repeated conversions\\n- Spawns goroutines in a `sync.WaitGroup` for each webhook\\n- Each goroutine independently calls its webhook via `callHook()`\\n- Collects errors in a channel for centralized error handling\\n- Includes panic recovery and crash handling per goroutine\\n- Supports failure policy (Ignore or Fail) with independent evaluation per goroutine\\n\\nThis parallel design improves latency since validating webhooks don't modify the object.\\n\\n## Configuration Management\\n\\nThe configuration managers in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/configuration/` serve as the `Source` for webhooks:\\n\\n- `NewMutatingWebhookConfigurationManager`: Reads `MutatingWebhookConfiguration` objects from a Kubernetes informer, creates `mutatingWebhookAccessor` instances, maintains a cache, and provides sorted lists of webhooks\\n- `NewValidatingWebhookConfigurationManager`: Similarly manages `ValidatingWebhookConfiguration` objects\\n\\nBoth managers implement:\\n- Lazy evaluation of webhook configurations\\n- Caching of created webhook accessors (expensive due to CEL expression compilation)\\n- Event handlers for Add/Update/Delete of configurations\\n- Deterministic ordering of webhooks across configurations\\n\\n## API Type Definitions\\n\\nIn `admissionregistration/v1/types.go` and `admissionregistration/v1beta1/types.go`, the Kubernetes API defines:\\n\\n- `MutatingWebhookConfiguration`: A cluster-scoped resource containing multiple `MutatingWebhook` objects. Each webhook specifies rules, failure policy, client configuration, reinvocation policy, side effects, and match conditions.\\n- `ValidatingWebhookConfiguration`: A cluster-scoped resource containing multiple `ValidatingWebhook` objects with similar fields but no reinvocation policy.\\n- `MutatingWebhook` and `ValidatingWebhook`: Individual webhook specifications with support for namespace/object selectors, rule matching, and CEL-based match conditions.\\n\\n## Processing Flow Summary\\n\\n**Mutating Webhooks**:\\n1. Plugin.Admit() \u2192 Webhook.Dispatch() \u2192 mutatingDispatcher.Dispatch()\\n2. Serial processing of webhooks (deterministic ordering)\\n3. Each webhook may modify the object (patch)\\n4. Reinvocation support when objects change\\n5. Result: Modified object passed to next plugin\\n\\n**Validating Webhooks**:\\n1. Plugin.Validate() \u2192 Webhook.Dispatch() \u2192 validatingDispatcher.Dispatch()\\n2. Parallel processing of webhooks (spawn goroutines)\\n3. Each webhook validates without modification\\n4. First error returned (early failure)\\n5. Result: Accept/reject decision\\n\\nBoth pipelines share the same generic webhook matching logic (ShouldCallHook) and WebhookAccessor abstraction, ensuring consistent behavior across mutating and validating webhooks while allowing pipeline-specific optimizations.\"\n}\n",
